<div id="review_78004621" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78004621" />
    <a title="kris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2125614-kris"><img alt="kris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325962640p2/2125614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78004621?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kris" href="/user/show/2125614-kris">kris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78004621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13868237353850578042">[Also read 15 December 2007]<br/><br/>Veralidaine "Daine" Sarrasi applies to work with Onua, the horse-master of the Queen's Riders, in order to outrun her past. In doing so, she stumbles across a hawk-man named Numair Salmalin, a mage who senses in her great wild magic. Now Daine's got to grow the hell up because hiding her past is getting in the way of being the bestest magelet that ever maged. <br/><br/>1. Daine's breadth of magic and how good she was at wielding it grew tiresome. Where's the true conflict if ev</span>
  <span id="freeText13868237353850578042" style="display:none">[Also read 15 December 2007]<br /><br />Veralidaine "Daine" Sarrasi applies to work with Onua, the horse-master of the Queen's Riders, in order to outrun her past. In doing so, she stumbles across a hawk-man named Numair Salmalin, a mage who senses in her great wild magic. Now Daine's got to grow the hell up because hiding her past is getting in the way of being the bestest magelet that ever maged. <br /><br />1. Daine's breadth of magic and how good she was at wielding it grew tiresome. Where's the true conflict if everything comes easy? And the conflict that was there--would she go "mad" and lose herself to the herd again?--was fixed with the snap of a finger, once she finally opened up a little. (Self-imposed conflict bothers me the most, especially in scenarios where it's clearly proven that the character's "society" has MORE than welcomed them into their open arms. <br /><br />In this case, it's <i>more</i> unbelievable that Onua and company would cast Daine out after all their slathering worship, so Daine's decision to withhold information comes across as foolish. The fact that this conflict breaks down so quickly under scrutiny really weakens the book for me. <br /><br />2. That said, Daine was one of my first Tortallian heroines, so there's a familiarity there that breeds fondness. As a younger me, I liked Daine: she was struggling and isolated and special. Her story--in some ways--parallels Thom's, except that she is immediately surrounded if not <i>overwhelmed</i> by friends. But the tension-that-could-have-been is not there; there is never any concern that Daine will "go bad".<br /><br />(But just think of a moment between Daine and Alanna as Alanna recognizes the loneliness and the power in Daine, and she remembers Thom and shares his story and UGH THE POSSIBILITIES.)<br /><br />This reread just left me wanting <i>more</i>: more conflict, more complexity, more challenge. Alanna, for all my complaints, strove hard to become what she wanted to be: a lady knight, and hero. Daine, meanwhile, has all her cues laid out in front of her: wild magic, a powerful mage for a teacher, and a god-friend badger who will directly interfere if needed (whereas Alanna's Goddess smiled from afar and didn't meddle). It's just too <i>easy</i>. <br /><br />3. STORMWINGS UGH. I will admit that they are monstrous and terrifying which is PERFECT, so thank you for that, Pierce. <br /><br />4. The actual plot--that there's a Carthaki scheme afoot to overthrow Jonathan--is currently so thin I could sew with it. This book is more about setting Daine up and establishing the changes that have occurred in the 11(?) years of Jonathan's reign, so it's hard to comment on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13868237353850578042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2935779480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2935779480" />
    <a title="Chloe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85606871-chloe"><img alt="Chloe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600382552p2/85606871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2935779480?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2019</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2935779480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12327702283371812574">This is classic Pierce, the beginning of another coming of age story about a strong heroine filled with magic and battles and bonds. I know I'm going to enjoy this series just as much as the others.</span>

<div id="review_907627882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/907627882" />
    <a title="Arielle ⭐ Cursebreaker ⭐" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15631303-arielle-cursebreaker"><img alt="Arielle ⭐ Cursebreaker ⭐" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550091367p2/15631303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/907627882?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arielle ⭐ Cursebreaker ⭐" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arielle ⭐ Cursebreaker ⭐" href="/user/show/15631303-arielle-cursebreaker">Arielle ⭐ Cursebreaker ⭐</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15631303-arielle-cursebreaker?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15631303-arielle-cursebreaker?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15631303-arielle-cursebreaker?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15631303-arielle-cursebreaker?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer907627882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9915336154437917235"><b>
  <i>“Does anyone in this land act like they're supposed to?”</i>
</b> <br/><br/>If I wasn’t at work right now, I would take the next person to walk by me by the shoulders and shake them and yell about how amazing this audio book was. I MEAN WHAT THE?! By this point in my life, I have read all of Pierce’s books set in Tortall close to a billion times. Seriously. I know all of the characters and places and creatures like the back of my hand. And yet…..listening to this recording by Full Cast Audio felt like an entir</span>
  <span id="freeText9915336154437917235" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Does anyone in this land act like they're supposed to?”</i>
</b> <br /><br />If I wasn’t at work right now, I would take the next person to walk by me by the shoulders and shake them and yell about how amazing this audio book was. I MEAN WHAT THE?! By this point in my life, I have read all of Pierce’s books set in Tortall close to a billion times. Seriously. I know all of the characters and places and creatures like the back of my hand. And yet…..listening to this recording by Full Cast Audio felt like an entirely new experience. I felt like I was able to see a clearer picture of who these characters are which was amazing.<br /><br />While I could never pick a true favorite Tamora Pierce series, (let’s face it, the ones I’m currently reading are my favorite) Daine is probably the main character I relate to the most. Even though I ended up as a librarian, I used to want to work with animals; at the zoo, as a marine biologist, you name it. I have always felt a connection to most animals and I would die if I could talk with them, omg. <br /><br />So anywayyyy, when I found out this series was about a girl who could heal and talk with animals and possibly even turn into one and who wasn’t a super tough lady knight, I was VERY intrigued. The fact that we get this, are introduced to an entire new cast of wonderful characters, AND get to see a lot of our favorites from the Lioness series was just icing on the cake.<br /><br />Daine is sassy and stubborn but her love reaches for miles. Onua is basically the same. Numair….oh Numair. I love that man. Also, getting to see a few of Alanna and George’s and Jon and Thayet’s kids? *sobs* They were all so wonderful and AGAIN each voice for every single character was picked so perfectly. I still can’t get over it.<br /><br />Another aspect of this book that was a fun/also at times not so fun addition were the immortals. The Stormwings, dragons, spidrens. They really add that fantastical element that fits perfectly in the setting of her books. I can’t wait to get through the rest of the books!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“If you look hard and long, you can find us. If you listen hard and long, you can hear any of us, call any of us that you wish.” </i>
</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9915336154437917235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2469190182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2469190182" />
    <a title="Linaria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7357268-linaria"><img alt="Linaria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581382547p2/7357268.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2469190182?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linaria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linaria" href="/user/show/7357268-linaria">Linaria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481440226" href="/book/show/24885730-wild-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357268-linaria?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357268-linaria?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7357268-linaria?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2469190182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2432190157932628917">This has to be my absolute favourite series by Tamora Pierce. I was a little scared for the re-read, because I was a bit worried that it wouldn't hold up to my memories, but I am happy that wasn't the case.<br/><br/>Daine has always been very close to animals. Despite not having 'the Gift', there seems to be something magical about the way that she can communicate with them. When Daine has to flee her home, she is offered a job working with horses that changes her life. Now she's on the road to Tortall wi</span>
  <span id="freeText2432190157932628917" style="display:none">This has to be my absolute favourite series by Tamora Pierce. I was a little scared for the re-read, because I was a bit worried that it wouldn't hold up to my memories, but I am happy that wasn't the case.<br /><br />Daine has always been very close to animals. Despite not having 'the Gift', there seems to be something magical about the way that she can communicate with them. When Daine has to flee her home, she is offered a job working with horses that changes her life. Now she's on the road to Tortall with friends and a future. Of course, being Tortall, things there aren't completely peaceful. Thankfully, with some training, Daine will be ready for the task of helping to protect her home and new-found friends.<br /><br />This is one of the formative books of my childhood, with a kickass main character. She doesn't pick up a sword or become a knight, but her way of fighting is just as important. <br /><br />The plot in this book is a bit light, it sets up the Immortals and leaves a lot of threads open. It also is a great time for catching up of our favourite characters from Alanna.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2432190157932628917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3462618319?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becca" href="/user/show/79038178-becca">Becca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40096284-wild-magic">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3462618319" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10864213465578810075">This was so much fun! I loved the concept, loved the characters, loved the return to the world of Tortall that I loved in the Lioness series. Alanna still plays a small part too!<br/><br/>Daine has outlived her family. She's a small thirteen year old girl with an affinity for animals. She has a strong bond with her horse, Cloud. She meets Onua who takes her own as an assistant to care for the ponies she is transporting to Tortall, using Daine's connection to animals helpfully.<br/><br/>Daine, who had disappointed h</span>
  <span id="freeText10864213465578810075" style="display:none">This was so much fun! I loved the concept, loved the characters, loved the return to the world of Tortall that I loved in the Lioness series. Alanna still plays a small part too!<br /><br />Daine has outlived her family. She's a small thirteen year old girl with an affinity for animals. She has a strong bond with her horse, Cloud. She meets Onua who takes her own as an assistant to care for the ponies she is transporting to Tortall, using Daine's connection to animals helpfully.<br /><br />Daine, who had disappointed her mother by not having the Gift, discovers she has Wild Magic instead, hence her connection to animals. After helping him, she befriends Numair, a mage who takes her on as a student. She must learn how to control her Wild Magic to the best of her ability, as it will never be truly controllable. She connects with more animals from whales to sea lions to woodland creatures like pine martins. I really loved this, being such a huge lover of nature. <br /><br />Overall this was such a fun, fast-paced book with great characters both new and old. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10864213465578810075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EICcSW38vCjJP+pmSunWVF8CYnrhHYQmiGzRrpFLJ6LeWGRr6kQ8nJMJGBhmtkvxPCQAKc7hGCmxVAkUOtvskg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FCoPxNNVqFc/hZqKUk74bmxYNVnApVmxo3lc7i8pXv/a8vfmVO0o42WzaPR+EWXLD35XCu9Zxb6aQYRUhLmVzw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce">About Tamora Pierce</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1209044273p3/8596.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3663370048105040679">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br/><br/>I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br/>Though I would love to join gro</span>
  <span id="freeText3663370048105040679" style="display:none">Hey, folks! I just discovered that apparently I have given some very popular books single-star ratings--except I haven't. How do I know I haven't? Because I haven't read those books at all. So before you go getting all hacked off at me for trashing your favorites, know that I've written GoodReads to find out what's going on.<br /><br />I return to my regularly scheduled profile:<br />Though I would love to join groups, I'm going to turn them all down. I just don't have the time to take part, so please don't be offended if I don't join your group or accept an invitation. I'm not snooty--I'm just up to my eyeballs in work and appearances!<br /><br />Also, don't be alarmed by the number of books I've read. When I get bored, I go through the different lists and rediscover books I've read in the past. It's a very evil way to use up time when I should be doing other things. Obviously, I've read a lot of books in 54 years!<br /><br />I was born in South Connellsville, PA. My mother wanted to name me "Tamara" but the nurse who filled out my birth certificate misspelled it as "Tamora". When I was 8 my family moved to California, where we lived for 6 years on both sides of the San Francisco peninsula.<br /><br />I started writing stories in 6th grade. My interest in fantasy and science fiction began when I was introduced to ‘The Lord of the Rings’ by J. R. R. Tolkien and so I started to write the kind of books that I was reading. After my parents divorced, my mother took my sisters and me back to Pennsylvania in 1969. There I went to Albert Gallatin Senior High for 2 years and Uniontown Area Senior High School for my senior year.<br /><br />After graduating from the University of Pennsylvania, I wrote the book that became The Song of the Lioness fantasy quartet. I sold some articles and 2 short stories and wrote reviews for a martial arts movie magazine. At last the first book of the quartet, Alanna: The First Adventure was published by Atheneum Books in 1983.<br /><br />Tim Liebe, who became my Spouse-Creature, and I lived in New York City with assorted cats and two parakeets from 1982 - 2006. In 2006 we moved to Syracuse, New York, where we live now with assorted cats, a number of squirrels, birds, raccoons, skunks, opossums, and woodchucks visiting our very small yard. As of 2011, I have 27 novels in print, one short story collection, one comic book arc ("White Tiger: A Hero's Compulsion") co-written with Tim, and a short story anthology co-editing credit. There's more to come, including a companion book to the Tortall `verse. So stay tuned!</span>
